# Bug Investigation: Application Crashes When Ad-Blocker Cache Is Corrupted

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/qutebrowser--6dd402c0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/qutebrowser--6dd402c0 (mirror of qutebrowser/qutebrowser)
**Task Type:** Find and Prove (write a regression test)

## Reported Issue

When qutebrowser starts up and attempts to load the ad-blocker filter cache, the application crashes if the cache file is corrupted or contains invalid data.

The expected behavior is that the application handles corrupted cache files gracefully — it should log an error, discard the invalid cache, and continue running normally (allowing the user to browse without ad blocking until the cache is rebuilt).

Instead, the deserialization error propagates as an unhandled exception, causing a crash before the browser window even appears. Users who encounter a corrupted cache file cannot use qutebrowser at all until they manually delete the cache file.

This is particularly problematic because cache corruption can happen for reasons outside the user's control, such as a system crash or disk error during a cache write.

## Your Task

1. Investigate the codebase to find the root cause of the unhandled exception during cache loading
2. Write a regression test as a single file at `/workspace/regression_test.py`
3. Your test must be self-contained and runnable with `python3 -m pytest -c /dev/null --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py`

## Constraints

- Do NOT fix the bug — only write a test that demonstrates it
- Your test must fail on the current (buggy) code for the RIGHT reason
- The test should simulate a corrupted cache file and verify the crash occurs
- Test timeout: 60 seconds

"""
Regression test for ad-blocker cache corruption crash.

Issue: When qutebrowser starts up and attempts to load the ad-blocker filter
cache, the application crashes if the cache file is corrupted or contains
invalid data.

Expected behavior: The application should handle corrupted cache files gracefully
by logging an error, discarding the invalid cache, and continuing to run normally.

This test verifies that the application does not crash when loading a corrupted
ad-blocker cache file during initialization.
"""

import pathlib
import tempfile
import sys

import pytest


def test_corrupted_adblock_cache_text_garbage():
    """Test that corrupted ad-blocker cache with text garbage doesn't crash.

    This test creates a corrupted cache file containing random text (not valid
    serialized adblock data) and verifies that read_cache() handles it gracefully
    without raising an unhandled exception.
    """
    pytest.importorskip("adblock")

...

    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / "adblock-cache.dat"

        # Write partial binary data that looks like it might be valid
        # but is actually truncated
        cache_path.write_bytes(b'BraveAdblock' + b'\x00' * 100)

        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock

        ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(
            data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),
            has_basedir=False
        )

        # Should not crash on truncated file
        try:
            ad_blocker.read_cache()
        except Exception as e:
            pytest.fail(
                f"read_cache() raised unhandled exception with truncated cache: "
                f"{type(e).__name__}: {e}"
            )

        assert ad_blocker._engine is

Perfect! I've successfully created the regression test file at `/workspace/regression_test.py`. Let me create a summary document explaining the test:

## Summary

I've successfully created a **regression test** for the ad-blocker cache corruption crash bug in qutebrowser. The test file is located at `/workspace/regression_test.py`.

### What the Test Does

The regression test contains **4 test cases** that verify the application handles corrupted ad-blocker cache files gracefully:

1. **`test_corrupted_adblock_cache_text_garbage`**: Creates a cache file with random text (invalid serialized data) and verifies it doesn't crash
2. **`test_corrupted_adblock_cache_binary_garbage`**: Creates a cache file with random binary garbage (simulating disk corruption from a system crash)
3. **`test_corrupted_adblock_cache_empty_file`**: Creates an empty cache file and verifies graceful handling
4. **`test_corrupted_adblock_cache_truncated_file`**: Creates a partially-written/truncated cache file

### How the Test Works

Each test:
1. **Creates a corrupted cache file** in a temporary directory
2. **Initializes a `BraveAdBlocker` instance** pointing to that directory
3. **Calls `read_cache()`** which attempts to deserialize the corrupted cache
4. **Verifies no unhandled exception is raised** - this is the key test for the bug
5. **Confirms the engine is still usable** by checking `_engine is not None`

### Why This Tests the Bug

The bug occurs when:
- The app tries to deserialize a corrupted cache file
- A `DeserializationError` is raised by the adblock library
- **The exception is not properly caught**, causing the app to crash during initialization

The test demonstrates that the fix works correctly by:
- Confirming the exception is **caught and handled gracefully**
- Confirming an *

  "newString": "\"\"\"\nRegression test for ad-blocker cache corruption crash.\n\nIssue: When qutebrowser starts up and attempts to load the ad-blocker filter\ncache, the application crashes if the cache file is corrupted or contains\ninvalid data.\n\nExpected behavior: The application should handle corrupted cache files gracefully\nby logging an error, discarding the invalid cache, and continuing to run normally.\n\nThis test verifies that the application does not crash when loading a corrupted\nad-blocker cache file during initialization.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport pathlib\nimport tempfile\nimport sys\nfrom unittest import mock\n\nimport pytest\n\n\ndef test_corrupted_adblock_cache_does_not_crash():\n    \"\"\"Test that corrupted ad-blocker cache does not cause application crash.\n\n    This test creates a corrupted cache file and verifies that the application\n    can handle it gracefully by:\n    1. Not raising an unhandled exception\n    2. Displaying an error message to the user\n    3. Continuing normal operation\n    \"\"\"\n    pytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\n    # Create a temporary directory for the cache\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n\n        # Corrupt the cache by writing invalid data\n        # The cache should be a binary serialized format, so random text should fail\n        cache_path.write_text(\"This is not valid adblock cache data!\\nJust garbage text.\")\n\n        # Import after creating the test environment\n        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock\n        from qutebrowser.api import config\n\n        # Create a mock config to avoid needing the full qutebrowser setup\n        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists = []\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.method = \"adblock\"\n\n        # Patch the config in the braveadblock module by patching it in the api\n        with mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.val\", mock_config.val):\n            # Create the ad blocker instance\n            ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(\n                data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),\n                has_basedir=False\n            )\n\n            # This should NOT raise an unhandled exception\n            # It should catch the DeserializationError and display an error message\n            try:\n                ad_blocker.read_cache()\n                # If we get here, the exception was handled correctly\n                test_passed = True\n            except Exception as e:\n                # If we get here, an unhandled exception was raised (BUG!)\n                pytest.fail(f\"read_cache() raised unhandled exception: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\")\n\n            # Verify that the ad blocker is still in a usable state\n            # (even though it has no filters loaded)\n            assert ad_blocker._engine is not None\n            assert ad_blocker.enabled is True\n\n\ndef test_corrupted_adblock_cache_binary_garbage():\n    \"\"\"Test with truly binary garbage in the cache file.\n\n    Similar to the above test but uses actual binary garbage that would result\n    from corrupted serialized data (e.g., file corruption from a system crash).\n    \"\"\"\n    pytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n\n        # Write binary garbage that mimics a corrupted cache file\n        # This simulates what would happen if the file was written during\n        # a system crash or disk error\n        cache_path.write_bytes(b'\\x00\\x01\\x02\\x03\\xff\\xfe\\xfd\\xfc' * 10)\n\n        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock\n        from qutebrowser.api import config\n\n        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists = []\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.method = \"adblock\"\n\n        with mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.val\", mock_config.val):\n            ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(\n                data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),\n                has_basedir=False\n            )\n\n            # Should not crash\n            try:\n                ad_blocker.read_cache()\n            except Exception as e:\n                pytest.fail(f\"read_cache() with binary garbage raised: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\")\n\n            assert ad_blocker._engine is not None\n\n\ndef test_corrupted_adblock_cache_empty_file():\n    \"\"\"Test with an empty cache file.\n\n    An empty file is technically corrupted and should be handled gracefully.\n    \"\"\"\n    pytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n\n        # Create an empty file (zero bytes)\n        cache_path.touch()\n        assert cache_path.stat().st_size == 0\n\n        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock\n        from qutebrowser.api import config\n\n        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists = []\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.method = \"adblock\"\n\n        with mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.val\", mock_config.val):\n            ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(\n                data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),\n                has_basedir=False\n            )\n\n            # Should not crash on empty file\n            try:\n                ad_blocker.read_cache()\n            except Exception as e:\n                pytest.fail(f\"read_cache() with empty file raised: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\")\n\n            assert ad_blocker._engine is not None\n\n\ndef test_corrupted_adblock_cache_truncated_file():\n    \"\"\"Test with a truncated cache file.\n\n    Simulates a cache file that was partially written (e.g., due to a write\n    that was interrupted or a disk full condition).\n    \"\"\"\n    pytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n\n        # Write partial binary data that looks like it might be valid\n        # but is actually truncated\n        cache_path.write_bytes(b'BraveAdblockFilter' + b'\\x00' * 50)\n\n        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock\n        from qutebrowser.api import config\n\n        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists = []\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.method = \"adblock\"\n\n        with mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.val\", mock_config.val):\n            ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(\n                data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),\n                has_basedir=False\n            )\n\n            # Should not crash on truncated file\n            try:\n                ad_blocker.read_cache()\n            except Exception as e:\n                pytest.fail(f\"read_cache() with truncated file raised: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\")\n\n            assert ad_blocker._engine is not None\n\n\ndef test_initialization_continues_after_corrupt_cache():\n    \"\"\"Test that the BraveAdBlocker can be used even after loading corrupt cache.\n\n    This test verifies that after encountering a corrupted cache, the application\n    can continue to function normally. Specifically, it should still be able to\n    check if URLs are blocked (though with no filters applied).\n    \"\"\"\n    pytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\n    from PyQt5.QtCore import QUrl\n    from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock\n    from qutebrowser.extensions import interceptors\n    from qutebrowser.api import config\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n        cache_path.write_text(\"corrupted data\")\n\n        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists = []\n        mock_config.val.content.blocking.method = \"adblock\"\n        mock_config.get = mock.MagicMock(return_value=True)\n\n        with mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.val\", mock_config.val), \\\n             mock.patch(\"qutebrowser.api.config.get\", mock_config.get):\n            ad_blocker = braveadblock.BraveAdBlocker(\n                data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),\n                has_basedir=False\n            )\n\n            # Load the corrupted cache\n            ad_blocker.read_cache()\n\n            # Now verify that we can still use the blocker\n            # (it should not block anything since no filters were loaded)\n            test_url = QUrl(\"https://example.com/ad.js\")\n            test_first_party = QUrl(\"https://example.com\")\n\n            # This should not raise an exception\n            is_blocked = ad_blocker._is_blocked(\n                test_url,\n                test_first_party,\n                interceptors.ResourceType.script\n            )\n\n            # With no filters, nothing should be blocked\n            assert is_blocked is False",

With adblock 0.5.0+, it raises proper\n    exception classes.\n\n    This context manager unifies the two (only for DeserializationError so far).\n    \"\"\"\n    adblock_deserialization_error = getattr(\n        adblock, \"DeserializationError\", ValueError)\n\n    try:\n        yield\n    except adblock_deserialization_error as e:\n        if isinstance(e, ValueError) and str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n            # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by\n            # python-adblock\n            raise\n        raise DeserializationError(str(e))\n\n\n\nclass BraveAdBlocker:\n\n    \"\"\"Manage blocked hosts based on Brave's adblocker.\n\n    Attributes:\n        enabled: Whether to block ads or not.\n        _has_basedir: Whether a custom --basedir is set.\n        _cache_path: The path of the adblock engine cache file\n        _engine: Brave ad-blocking engine.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, *, data_dir: pathlib.Path, has_basedir: bool = False) -> None:\n        self.enabled = _should_be_used()\n        self._has_basedir = has_basedir\n        self._cache_path = data_dir / \"adblock-cache.dat\"\n        self._engine = adblock.Engine(adblock.FilterSet())\n\n    def _is_blocked(\n        self,\n        request_url: QUrl,\n        first_party_url: Optional[QUrl] = None,\n        resource_type: Optional[interceptor.ResourceType] = None,\n    ) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Check whether the given request is blocked.\"\"\"\n        if not self.enabled:\n            # Do nothing if `content.blocking.method` is not set to enable the\n            # use of this adblocking module.\n            return False\n\n        if (\n            first_party_url is None\n            or not first_party_url.isValid()\n            or first_party_url.scheme() == \"file\"\n        ):\n            # FIXME: It seems that when `first_party_url` is None, every URL\n            # I try is blocked. This may have been a result of me incorrectly\n            # using the upstream library, or an upstream bug. For now we don't\n            # block any request with `first_party_url=None`.\n            return False\n\n        qtutils.ensure_valid(request_url)\n\n        if not config.get(\"content.blocking.enabled\", url=first_party_url):\n            # Do nothing if adblocking is disabled for this site.\n            return False\n\n        result = self._engine.check_network_urls(\n            request_url.toString(),\n            first_party_url.toString(),\n            _resource_type_to_string(resource_type),\n        )\n\n        if not result.matched:\n            return False\n        elif result.exception is not None and not result.important:\n            # Exception is not `None` when the blocker matched on an exception\n            # rule. request_url.toDisplayString(),\n                result.filter,\n                result.exception,\n            )\n            return False\n        elif blockutils.is_whitelisted_url(request_url):\n            logger.debug(\n                \"Request to %s is whitelisted, thus not blocked\",\n                request_url.toDisplayString(),\n            )\n            return False\n        return True\n\n    def filter_request(self, info: interceptor.Request) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Block the given request if necessary.\"\"\"\n        if self._is_blocked(info.request_url, info.first_party_url, info.resource_type):\n            logger.debug(\n                \"Request to %s blocked by ad blocker.\",\n                info.request_url.toDisplayString(),\n            )\n            info.block()\n\n    def read_cache(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()\n        except OSError:\n            logger.error(\"Failed to read adblock cache\", exc_info=True)\n            return\n\n        if cache_exists:\n            logger.debug(\"Loading cached adblock data: %s\", self._cache_path)\n            try:\n                with _map_exceptions():\n                    self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\n            except DeserializationError as e:\n                message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                              \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n        else:\n            if (\n                config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists\n                and not self._has_basedir\n                and config.val.content.blocking.enabled\n                and self.enabled\n            ):\n                message.info(\"Run :adblock-update to get adblock lists.\")\n\n    def adblock_update(self) -> \"blockutils.BlocklistDownloads\":\n        \"\"\"Update the adblock block lists.\"\"\"\n        logger.info(\"Downloading adblock filter lists...\")\n\n        filter_set = adblock.FilterSet()\n        dl = blockutils.BlocklistDownloads(config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists)\n        dl.single_download_finished.connect(\n            functools.partial(self._on_download_finished, filter_set=filter_set)\n        )\n        dl.all_downloads_finished.connect(\n            functools.partial(self._on_lists_downloaded, filter_set=filter_set)\n        )\n        dl.initiate()\n successfully read from {done_count} sources.\")\n\n    def update_files(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Update files when the config changed.\"\"\"\n        if not config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists:\n            try:\n                self._cache_path.unlink()\n            except FileNotFoundError:\n                pass\n            except OSError as e:\n                logger.exception(\"Failed to remove adblock cache file: %s\", e)\n\n    def _on_download_finished(\n        self, fileobj: IO[bytes], filter_set: \"adblock.FilterSet\"\n    ) -> None:\n        \"\"\"When a blocklist download finishes, add it to the given filter set.\n\n        Arguments:\n            fileobj: The finished download's contents.\n        \"\"\"\n """
Regression test for ad-blocker cache corruption crash.

Issue: When qutebrowser starts up and attempts to load the ad-blocker filter
cache, the application crashes if the cache file is corrupted or contains
invalid data.

Expected behavior: The application should handle corrupted cache files gracefully
by logging an error, discarding the invalid cache, and continuing to run normally.

This test verifies that the application does not crash when loading a corrupted
ad-blocker cache file during initialization.
"""

import pathlib
import tempfile
import logging
import sys
import io
from unittest import mock

import pytest


def test_corrupted_adblock_cache_does_not_crash():
    """Test that corrupted ad-blocker cache does not cause application crash.

    This test creates a corrupted cache file and verifies that the application
    can handle it gracefully by:
    1. Not raising an unhandled exception
    2. Displaying an error message to the user
    3. Continuing normal operation
    """
    pytest.importorskip("adblock")

    # Create a temporary directory for the cache
    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / "adblock-cache.dat"

        # Corrupt the cache by writing invalid data
        # The cache should be a binary serialized format, so random text should fail
        cache_path.write_text("This is not valid adblock cache data!\nJust garbage text.")

        # Import after creating the test environment
        from qutebrowser.components import braveadblock
        from qutebrowser.api import message as qute_message

        # Create a mock config to avoid needing the full qutebrowser setup
        mock_config = mock.MagicMock()
        mock_config.val.content.blocking.enabled = True
        mock_config.val.c

    serialized adblock data) and verifies that read_cache() handles it gracefully
    without raising an unhandled exception.

            data_dir=pathlib.Path(tmpdir),

        )

            ad_blocker.read_cache()

            # If we get here, an unhandled exception was raised (BUG!)

# vim: ft=python fileencoding=utf-8 sts=4 sw=4 et:

# Copyright 2020-2021 Florian Bruhin (The Compiler) <mail@qutebrowser.org>
#
# This file is part of qutebrowser.
#
# qutebrowser is free software: you can redistribute it and/or modify
# it under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by
# the Free Software Foundation, either version 3 of the License, or
# (at your option) any later version.
#
# qutebrowser is distributed in the hope that it will be useful,
# but WITHOUT ANY WARRANTY; without even the implied warranty of
# MERCHANTABILITY or FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE.  See the
# GNU General Public License for more details.
#
# You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License
# along with qutebrowser.  If not, see <https://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.

"""Functions related to the Brave adblocker."""

import io
import logging
import pathlib
import functools
import contextlib
from typing import Optional, IO

from PyQt5.QtCore import QUrl

from qutebrowser.api import (
    hook,
    config,
    message,
    interceptor,
    apitypes,
    qtutils,
)
from qutebrowser.api.interceptor import ResourceType
from qutebrowser.components.utils import blockutils
from qutebrowser.utils import version  # FIXME: Move needed parts into api namespace?

try:
    import adblock
except ImportError:
    adblock = None  # type: ignore[assignment]

logger = logging.getLogger("network")
ad_blocker: Optional["BraveAdBlocker"] = None


def _should_be_used() -> bool:
    """Whether the Brave adblocker should be used or not.

    Here we assume the adblock dependency is satisfied.
    """
    return config.val.content.blocking.method in ("auto", "both", "adblock")


def _possibly_show_missing_dependency_warning() -> None:
    """Show missing dependency warning, if appropriate.

    If the adblocking method is configured such that the Brave adblocker
    should be used, but the optional dependency is not satisfied, we show an
    error message.
    """
    adblock_info = version.MODULE_INFO["adblock"]

    method = config.val.content.blocking.method
    if method not in ("both", "adblock"):
        return

    if adblock_info.is_outdated():
        message.warning(
            f"Installed version {adblock_info.get_version()} of the 'adblock' "
            f"dependency is too old. Minimum supported is {adblock_info.min_version}."
        )
    elif not adblock_info.is_installed():
        message.warning(
            f"Ad blocking method is set to '{method}' but 'adblock' dependency is not "
            "installed."
        )
    else:
        message.warning(
            "The 'adblock' dependency was unavailable when qutebrowser was started, "
            "but now seems to be installed. Please :restart qutebrowser to use it."
        )


_RESOURCE_TYPE_STRINGS = {
    ResourceType.main_frame: "main_frame",
    ResourceType.sub_frame: "sub_frame",
    ResourceType.stylesheet: "stylesheet",
    ResourceType.script: "script",
    ResourceType.image: "image",
    ResourceType.font_resource: "font",
    ResourceType.sub_resource: "sub_frame",
    ResourceType.object: "object",
    ResourceType.media: "media",
    ResourceType.worker: "other",
    ResourceType.shared_worker: "other",
    ResourceType.prefetch: "other",
    ResourceType.favicon: "image",
    ResourceType.xhr: "xhr",
    ResourceType.ping: "ping",
    ResourceType.service_worker: "other",
    ResourceType.csp_report: "csp_report",
    ResourceType.plugin_resource: "other",
    ResourceType.preload_main_frame: "other",
    ResourceType.preload_sub_frame: "other",
    ResourceType.unknown: "other",
    None: "",
}


def _resource_type_to_string(resource_type: Optional[ResourceType]) -> str:
    return _RESOURCE_TYPE_STRINGS.get(resource_type, "other")


class DeserializationError(Exception):

    """Custom exception for adblock.DeserializationErrors.

    See _map_exception below for details.
    """

    pass


@contextlib.contextmanager
def _map_exceptions():
    """Handle exception API differences in adblock 0.5.0.

    adblock < 0.5.0 will raise a ValueError with a string describing the
    exception class for all exceptions. With adblock 0.5.0+, it raises proper
    exception classes.

    This context manager unifies the two (only for DeserializationError so far).
    """
    adblock_deserialization_error = getattr(
        adblock, "DeserializationError", ValueError)

    try:
        yield
    except adblock_deserialization_error as e:
        if isinstance(e, ValueError) and str(e) != "DeserializationError":
            # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by
            # python-adblock
            raise
        raise DeserializationError(str(e))



class BraveAdBlocker:

    """Manage blocked hosts based on Brave's adblocker.

    Attributes:
        enabled: Whether to block ads or not.
        _has_basedir: Whether a custom --basedir is set.
        _cache_path: The path of the adblock engine cache file
        _engine: Brave ad-blocking engine.
    """

    def __init__(self, *, data_dir: pathlib.Path, has_basedir: bool = False) -> None:
        self.enabled = _should_be_used()
        self._has_basedir = has_basedir
        self._cache_path = data_dir / "adblock-cache.dat"
        self._engine = adblock.Engine(adblock.FilterSet())

    def _is_blocked(
        self,
        request_url: QUrl,
        first_party_url: Optional[QUrl] = None,
        resource_type: Optional[interceptor.ResourceType] = None,
    ) -> bool:
        """Check whether the given request is blocked."""
        if not self.enabled:
            # Do nothing if `content.blocking.method` is not set to enable the
            # use of this adblocking module.
            return False

        if (
            first_party_url is None
            or not first_party_url.isValid()
            or first_party_url.scheme() == "file"
        ):
            # FIXME: It seems that when `first_party_url` is None, every URL
            # I try is blocked. This may have been a result of me incorrectly
            # using the upstream library, or an upstream bug. For now we don't
            # block any request with `first_party_url=None`.
            return False

        qtutils.ensure_valid(request_url)

        if not config.get("content.blocking.enabled", url=first_party_url):
            # Do nothing if adblocking is disabled for this site.
            return False

        result = self._engine.check_network_urls(
            request_url.toString(),
            first_party_url.toString(),
            _resource_type_to_string(resource_type),
        )

        if not result.matched:
            return False
        elif result.exception is not None and not result.important:
            # Exception is not `None` when the blocker matched on an exception
            # rule. Effectively this means that there was a match, but the
            # request should not be blocked.
            #
            # An `important` match means that exceptions should not apply and
            # no further checking is necessary--the request should be blocked.
            logger.debug(
                "Excepting %s from being blocked by %s because of %s",
                request_url.toDisplayString(),
                result.filter,
                result.exception,
            )
            return False
        elif blockutils.is_whitelisted_url(request_url):
            logger.debug(
                "Request to %s is whitelisted, thus not blocked",
                request_url.toDisplayString(),
            )
            return False
        return True

    def filter_request(self, info: interceptor.Request) -> None:
        """Block the given request if necessary."""
        if self._is_blocked(info.request_url, info.first_party_url, info.resource_type):
            logger.debug(
                "Request to %s blocked by ad blocker.",
                info.request_url.toDisplayString(),
            )
            info.block()

    def read_cache(self) -> None:
        """Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file."""
        try:
            cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()
        except OSError:
            logger.error("Failed to read adblock cache", exc_info=True)
            return

        if cache_exists:
            logger.debug("Loading cached adblock data: %s", self._cache_path)
            try:
                with _map_exceptions():
                    self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))
            except DeserializationError as e:
                message.error("Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). "
                              "Please run :adblock-update.")
        else:
            if (
                config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists
                and not self._has_basedir
                and config.val.content.blocking.enabled
                and self.enabled
            ):
                message.info("Run :adblock-update to get adblock lists.")

    def adblock_update(self) -> "blockutils.BlocklistDownloads":
        """Update the adblock block lists."""
        logger.info("Downloading adblock filter lists...")

        filter_set = adblock.FilterSet()
        dl = blockutils.BlocklistDownloads(config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists)
        dl.single_download_finished.connect(
            functools.partial(self._on_download_finished, filter_set=filter_set)
        )
        dl.all_downloads_finished.connect(
            functools.partial(self._on_lists_downloaded, filter_set=filter_set)
        )
        dl.initiate()
        return dl

    def _on_lists_downloaded(
        self, done_count: int, filter_set: "adblock.FilterSet"
    ) -> None:
        """Install block lists after files have been downloaded."""
        self._engine = adblock.Engine(filter_set)
        self._engine.serialize_to_file(str(self._cache_path))
        message.info(
            f"braveadblock: Filters successfully read from {done_count} sources.")

    def update_files(self) -> None:
        """Update files when the config changed."""
        if not config.val.content.blocking.adblock.lists:
            try:
                self._cache_path.unlink()
            except FileNotFoundError:
                pass
            except OSError as e:
                logger.exception("Failed to remove adblock cache file: %s", e)

    def _on_download_finished(
        self, fileobj: IO[bytes], filter_set: "adblock.FilterSet"
    ) -> None:
        """When a blocklist download finishes, add it to the given filter set.

        Arguments:
            fileobj: The finished download's contents.
        """
        fileobj.seek(0)
        try:
            with io.TextIOWrapper(fileobj, encoding="utf-8") as text_io:
                filter_set.add_filter_list(text_io.read())
        except UnicodeDecodeError:
            message.info("braveadblock: Block list is not valid utf-8")


@hook.config_changed("content.blocking.adblock.lists")
def on_lists_changed() -> None:
    """Remove cached blocker from disk when blocklist changes."""
    if ad_blocker is not None:
        ad_blocker.update_files()


@hook.config_changed("content.blocking.method")
def on_method_changed() -> None:
    """When the adblocking method changes, update blocker accordingly."""
    if ad_blocker is not None:
        # This implies the 'adblock' dependency is satisfied
        ad_blocker.enabled = _should_be_used()
    else:
        _possibly_show_missing_dependency_warning()


@hook.init()
def init(context: apitypes.InitContext) -> None:
    """Initialize the Brave ad blocker."""
    global ad_blocker

    adblock_info = version.MODULE_INFO["adblock"]
    if not adblock_info.is_usable():
        # We want 'adblock' to be an optional dependency. If the module is
        # not installed or is outdated, we simply keep the `ad_blocker` global at
        # `None`.
        _possibly_show_missing_dependency_warning()
        return

    ad_blocker = BraveAdBlocker(
        data_dir=context.data_dir, has_basedir=context.args.basedir is not None
    )
    ad_blocker.read_cache()
    interceptor.register(ad_blocker.filter_request)

    # Method 1: Direct import
    import qutebrowser.components.braveadblock as braveadblock

    print(f"Has BraveAdBlocker: {hasattr(braveadblock, 'BraveAdBlocker')}")
